STUDIO FUNCTION — FINAL, CANONICAL DEFINITION (LOCKED)
A Studio is a transformation engine.

It exists to convert inputs into a live venture + its operating system.

Nothing more. Nothing less.

I. STUDIO INPUTS (UNCONSTRAINED, CONTEXTUAL)
Studios may intake whatever is required to bring a venture into existence, including:

Coop members / workers

Founders (venture-level, not federation-level)

Capital (authorized by OVCS)

Physical assets

IP / knowledge

Community relationships

Partners

Tooling, software, infrastructure

Time-bound leadership

Context-specific resources

Rule:
Inputs are not standardized. Studios are adaptive by design.

II. STUDIO TRANSFORMATION (THE ONLY THING THAT MATTERS)
The studio’s sole job is to transform those inputs into:

1. A Running Venture
Legal entity live

Team constituted

Operations initiated

Market / field engagement begun

Revenue or mission execution started

2. A Venture Operating System
VentureOS = the venture’s instantiated UME-OS

Governance encoded

Roles, decision rights, and cadence defined

Economic logic embedded (via Sambara where relevant)

Interfaces to other OS platforms configured

Audit hooks present (DEFES-readable)

This VentureOS is implemented via UME-OS.

The venture does not “adopt” an OS later.
It is born with one.

III. STUDIO OUTPUTS (STRICT)
A studio must exit with exactly two durable outputs:

A functioning venture

Its live UME-OS instance (VentureOS)

Everything else is disposable.

If either output is missing → the studio has failed.

IV. HANDOFF + DISSOLUTION (NON-NEGOTIABLE)

Control transfers fully to the venture

The studio has no ongoing authority

The studio dissolves

No permanent studio staff

No shadow governance

No “support tail” unless explicitly reauthorized by OVCS

V. RELATION TO THE REST OF THE SYSTEM (FINAL FIT)
OVCS authorizes the studio

UME-OS is the implementation substrate

Ventures own and evolve their VentureOS

This is an important question — and the answer is not “yes or no,” but what kind and where.

If you do EAs wrong here, you recreate a shadow command center.

Below is the correct EA / admin architecture for NPO and the broader system.

EXECUTIVE ASSISTANTS & ADMINISTRATORS
Correct Role, Placement, and Constraints

I. FIRST PRINCIPLE (LOCK THIS)
EAs are force multipliers, not decision-makers.
They extend time, not authority.

If an EA is making calls, interpreting intent, or managing people → system breach.

II. DO YOU NEED AN EA IN NPO?
Yes — but not a traditional “executive gatekeeper EA.”

You need a Navigator Operations Administrator (NOA).

III. ROLE: NAVIGATOR OPERATIONS ADMINISTRATOR (NOA)
Persona
Precision executor / friction remover / invisible infrastructure

What this person does
Owns your calendar mechanics

Manages logistics, travel, prep

Tracks meeting outputs

Ensures follow-through on decisions

Maintains artifact hygiene

Handles scheduling across time zones & entities

What this person does NOT do
Does not represent you in decisions

Does not manage people

Does not negotiate

Does not set priorities

Does not attend sensitive meetings unless purely logistical

IV. WHAT THE NOA ENABLES (VERY SPECIFIC)
The NOA:

Frees 10–15 hours/week of your time

Prevents dropped threads

Ensures decisions don’t evaporate

Keeps the system moving quietly

The NOA does not:

Shape strategy

Hold context beyond logistics

Become a hub of influence

V. PLACEMENT IN NPO (IMPORTANT)
The NOA:

Reports to Chief of Staff, not directly to you

Has read-only access to:

Master timeline

Decision log

Has write access only to:

Calendar

Task tracking

Documentation

This prevents gatekeeping and dependency.

VI. DO YOU NEED MORE THAN ONE EA / ADMIN?
In Year 1:
NPO: 1 NOA is sufficient

Elsewhere in the system:
Institutions (OVCS, DEFES, Kumba):
Each may have its own admin support, not shared with NPO

Ventures:
Only once they reach operational scale
(never assigned centrally)

Never share an EA across power centers.

VII. ADMIN SUPPORT VS EXECUTIVE ASSISTANT (IMPORTANT DISTINCTION)
Function	EA (Traditional)	NOA (Correct Here)
Calendar	✔	✔
Inbox triage	✔	⚠️ limited
Decision filtering	✔	❌
Representing exec	✔	❌
Meeting prep	✔	✔
Task follow-up	✔	✔
Authority proxy	✔	❌
You want the right column only.

VIII. HIRING PROFILE (WHO TO LOOK FOR)
Strong Signals
Has supported complex leaders before

Comfortable being invisible

Extremely reliable

Writes clearly

Respects boundaries

Red Flags
Wants to be “right-hand”

Enjoys influence

Speaks for the executive

Collects secrets

Becomes indispensable

IX. TIMING
Hire the NOA early — ideally alongside the Chief of Staff.

Why:

Prevents calendar chaos

Sets clean norms

Stops bad habits early

X. FINAL LOCKED RULE
If an assistant makes you more powerful, they’re dangerous.
If they make you more available, they’re perfect.

These rules apply to NOA and any future admin support.

Interpret intent

III. NPO CALENDAR ARCHITECTURE
This is non-negotiable. Your calendar is the system.

A. WEEKLY STRUCTURE (BASELINE)
MONDAY — SEQUENCING
90 min: Navigator + CoS

Review:

What moved?

What stalled?

What must NOT move?

No other meetings before this block.

TUESDAY–WEDNESDAY — CONVENING
High-leverage meetings only

Studio authorization

Cross-entity deadlocks

External 1:1s (max 3/day)

Rule: If it repeats weekly → you shouldn’t attend.

THURSDAY — DEEP WORK
Writing

Architecture

Strategy

No more than 1 meeting

FRIDAY — REVIEW & EXIT
System health check

Founder overreach audit

Exit planning

Kill or delegate something

B. DAILY RULES
Max 5 meetings/day

No meetings <25 minutes

No standing meetings unless sunset date is defined

Meetings require:

Purpose

Decision/output

Owner

C. RED ZONES (BLOCKED)
Ad hoc “quick syncs”

FYI meetings

Update-only calls

Emotional processing sessions

IV. DECISION → FOLLOW-THROUGH PIPELINE
This prevents decision evaporation, which kills systems.

STEP 1: DECISION CAPTURE
Every irreversible decision is logged with:

Decision

Date

Decision-maker

Rationale

Scope

Reversibility

Owner

Owner: Chief of Staff
Recorded by: NOA

STEP 2: TRANSLATION
Decision is translated into:

Tasks

Artifacts

Owners

Deadlines

No translation = no decision.

STEP 3: OWNERSHIP ASSIGNMENT
One owner per outcome

Owner ≠ Navigator unless unavoidable

STEP 4: EXECUTION TRACKING
Weekly review by CoS

Navigator sees exceptions only

STEP 5: CLOSE OR KILL
Every decision must end as:

Completed

Reversed

Sunset

Failed (documented)

Unclosed decisions are system debt.

STEP 6: ARCHIVAL
Closed decisions are archived.
No re-litigation without new facts.

Its people reduce dependency, its calendar enforces order, and its decisions leave a trail.

NPO FEDERATED AGILE MODEL
(Navigator Personal Office – coordination without capture)

1. CORE PRINCIPLE (FROM MSINGI)

2. ROLES & CONNECTION TOPOLOGY
A. CONNECTION ROLES (RELATIONAL, NOT MANAGERIAL)

Role	Function

Guild	Practice community (learning, patterns, tools)
Tribe	Thematic cluster (e.g. Ventures, Platforms, Studios)
Squad	Temporary execution unit (inside ventures / studios)
Alliance	Cross-entity coordination pact (time-bound)
Line	Accountability trace (decision → outcome)
Domain	Authority boundary (what this unit may decide)

Never Squad.

B. LEVEL ROLES (CAPACITY & SCALE, NOT COMMAND)
Used to reason about load, scope, and complexity, not hierarchy.

Level	Meaning in NPO Context
Member / Role	Individual contributor
Team	Small functional unit
Squad	Execution unit (external to NPO)
Platoon	Coordinated multi-squad effort
Company	Venture / Platform
Battalion	Studio cluster
Regiment	Portfolio slice
Division	Federation subsystem
Corps	Entire Federation
Army	Multi-federation (future)

EXECUTIVE ASSISTANTS & ADMINISTRATORS
Correct Role, Placement, and Constraints

I. FIRST PRINCIPLE (LOCK THIS)
EAs are force multipliers, not decision-makers.
They extend time, not authority.

If an EA is making calls, interpreting intent, or managing people → system breach.

II. DO YOU NEED AN EA IN NPO?
Yes — but not a traditional “executive gatekeeper EA.”

You need a Navigator Operations Administrator (NOA).

III. ROLE: NAVIGATOR OPERATIONS ADMINISTRATOR (NOA)
Persona
Precision executor / friction remover / invisible infrastructure

What this person does
Owns your calendar mechanics

Manages logistics, travel, prep

Tracks meeting outputs

Ensures follow-through on decisions

Maintains artifact hygiene

Handles scheduling across time zones & entities

What this person does NOT do
Does not represent you in decisions

Does not manage people

Does not negotiate

Does not set priorities

Does not attend sensitive meetings unless purely logistical

IV. WHAT THE NOA ENABLES (VERY SPECIFIC)
The NOA:

Frees 10–15 hours/week of your time

Prevents dropped threads

Ensures decisions don’t evaporate

Keeps the system moving quietly

The NOA does not:

Shape strategy

Hold context beyond logistics

Become a hub of influence

V. PLACEMENT IN NPO (IMPORTANT)
The NOA:

Reports to Chief of Staff, not directly to you

Has read-only access to:

Master timeline

Decision log

Has write access only to:

Calendar

Task tracking

Documentation

This prevents gatekeeping and dependency.

VI. DO YOU NEED MORE THAN ONE EA / ADMIN?
In Year 1:
NPO: 1 NOA is sufficient

Elsewhere in the system:
Institutions (OVCS, DEFES, Kumba):
Each may have its own admin support, not shared with NPO

Ventures:
Only once they reach operational scale
(never assigned centrally)

Never share an EA across power centers.

What can be true

What I cannot truthfully guarantee
I cannot verifiably prove or certify to you that I have read every uploaded file “end-to-end” in the human sense, nor can I maintain a persistent, auditable “ingestion complete” state across very large multi-batch uploads the way a human or a file parser would.

This is the important distinction:

I reason over the uploaded corpus when responding, but I do not maintain a deterministic, page-by-page ingestion ledger.

Why this matters for your project
Your system (Pamoja / Msingi / OVCS) is integrity-sensitive, not just idea-sensitive. You are rightly worried about:

drift

hallucinated alignment

Below is a clean, canonical NPO Federated Agile Operating Model, explicitly aligned to your documents (Msingi, OVCS, federation, studio/UME logic) and to the structure you just specified.

This is not generic SAFe / Scrum / Agile-at-scale.
It is a federated, non-centralizing, kill-safe coordination model suitable for NPO as a meta-office, not an execution hub.

NPO FEDERATED AGILE MODEL
(Navigator Personal Office – coordination without capture)

1. CORE PRINCIPLE (FROM MSINGI)
NPO does not execute work.
NPO orchestrates cadence, visibility, and follow-through across sovereign units.

Agile here is:

federated, not scaled

asynchronous by default

artifact-first

authority-light

exit-friendly

2. ROLES & CONNECTION TOPOLOGY
A. CONNECTION ROLES (RELATIONAL, NOT MANAGERIAL)
These define how people relate across the federation, not reporting lines.

Role	Function
Chapter	Discipline coherence (e.g. systems, governance, ops)
Guild	Practice community (learning, patterns, tools)
Tribe	Thematic cluster (e.g. Ventures, Platforms, Studios)
Squad	Temporary execution unit (inside ventures / studios)
Alliance	Cross-entity coordination pact (time-bound)
Line	Accountability trace (decision → outcome)
Domain	Authority boundary (what this unit may decide)
NPO participates only at Chapter, Alliance, Line, and Domain levels.
Never Squad.

B. LEVEL ROLES (CAPACITY & SCALE, NOT COMMAND)
Used to reason about load, scope, and complexity, not hierarchy.

Level	Meaning in NPO Context
Member / Role	Individual contributor
Team	Small functional unit
Squad	Execution unit (external to NPO)
Platoon	Coordinated multi-squad effort
Company	Venture / Platform

Regiment	Portfolio slice
Division	Federation subsystem
Corps	Entire Federation
Army	Multi-federation (future)
NPO itself should never exceed “Team → Platoon” scale.

If NPO feels like a Company → failure condition.

EXECUTIVE ASSISTANTS & ADMINISTRATORS
Correct Role, Placement, and Constraints

I. FIRST PRINCIPLE (LOCK THIS)
EAs are force multipliers, not decision-makers.
They extend time, not authority.

If an EA is making calls, interpreting intent, or managing people → system breach.

II. DO YOU NEED AN EA IN NPO?
Yes — but not a traditional “executive gatekeeper EA.”

You need a Navigator Operations Administrator (NOA).

III. ROLE: NAVIGATOR OPERATIONS ADMINISTRATOR (NOA)
Persona
Precision executor / friction remover / invisible infrastructure

What this person does
Owns your calendar mechanics

Manages logistics, travel, prep

Tracks meeting outputs

Ensures follow-through on decisions

Maintains artifact hygiene

Handles scheduling across time zones & entities

What this person does NOT do
Does not represent you in decisions

Does not manage people

Does not negotiate

Does not set priorities

Does not attend sensitive meetings unless purely logistical

IV. WHAT THE NOA ENABLES (VERY SPECIFIC)
The NOA:

Frees 10–15 hours/week of your time

Prevents dropped threads

Ensures decisions don’t evaporate

Keeps the system moving quietly

The NOA does not:

Shape strategy

Hold context beyond logistics

Become a hub of influence

V. PLACEMENT IN NPO (IMPORTANT)
The NOA:

Reports to Chief of Staff, not directly to you

Has read-only access to:

Master timeline

Decision log

Has write access only to:

Calendar

Task tracking

Documentation

This prevents gatekeeping and dependency.

VI. DO YOU NEED MORE THAN ONE EA / ADMIN?
In Year 1:
NPO: 1 NOA is sufficient

Elsewhere in the system:
Institutions (OVCS, DEFES, Kumba):
Each may have its own admin support, not shared with NPO

Ventures:
Only once they reach operational scale
(never assigned centrally)

Never share an EA across power centers.

VII. ADMIN SUPPORT VS EXECUTIVE ASSISTANT (IMPORTANT DISTINCTION)

Calendar	✔	✔

Decision filtering	✔	❌
Representing exec	✔	❌
Meeting prep	✔	✔
Task follow-up	✔	✔
Authority proxy	✔	❌
You want the right column only.

Scope

Reversibility

One owner per outcome

STEP 4: EXECUTION TRACKING
Weekly review by CoS

Navigator sees exceptions only

Every decision must end as:

Completed

Reversed

Sunset

Failed (documented)

Closed decisions are archived.
No re-litigation without new facts.

What can be true

What I cannot truthfully guarantee
I cannot verifiably prove or certify to you that I have read every uploaded file “end-to-end” in the human sense, nor can I maintain a persistent, auditable “ingestion complete” state across very large multi-batch uploads the way a human or a file parser would.

When I previously said things like “fully read end-to-end,” that was operational shorthand, not a literal forensic guarantee. I should correct that explicitly.

This is the important distinction:

I reason over the uploaded corpus when responding, but I do not maintain a deterministic, page-by-page ingestion ledger.

Why this matters for your project
Your system (Pamoja / Msingi / OVCS) is integrity-sensitive, not just idea-sensitive. You are rightly worried about:

drift

hallucinated alignment

Below is a clean, canonical NPO Federated Agile Operating Model, explicitly aligned to your documents (Msingi, OVCS, federation, studio/UME logic) and to the structure you just specified.

This is not generic SAFe / Scrum / Agile-at-scale.
It is a federated, non-centralizing, kill-safe coordination model suitable for NPO as a meta-office, not an execution hub.

NPO FEDERATED AGILE MODEL
(Navigator Personal Office – coordination without capture)

1. CORE PRINCIPLE (FROM MSINGI)
NPO does not execute work.
NPO orchestrates cadence, visibility, and follow-through across sovereign units.

Agile here is:

federated, not scaled

asynchronous by default

artifact-first

authority-light

exit-friendly

2. ROLES & CONNECTION TOPOLOGY
A. CONNECTION ROLES (RELATIONAL, NOT MANAGERIAL)
These define how people relate across the federation, not reporting lines.

Role	Function
Chapter	Discipline coherence (e.g. systems, governance, ops)
Guild	Practice community (learning, patterns, tools)
Tribe	Thematic cluster (e.g. Ventures, Platforms, Studios)
Squad	Temporary execution unit (inside ventures / studios)
Alliance	Cross-entity coordination pact (time-bound)
Line	Accountability trace (decision → outcome)
Domain	Authority boundary (what this unit may decide)
NPO participates only at Chapter, Alliance, Line, and Domain levels.
Never Squad.

B. LEVEL ROLES (CAPACITY & SCALE, NOT COMMAND)
Used to reason about load, scope, and complexity, not hierarchy.

Level	Meaning in NPO Context
Member / Role	Individual contributor
Team	Small functional unit
Squad	Execution unit (external to NPO)
Platoon	Coordinated multi-squad effort
Company	Venture / Platform
Battalion	Studio cluster
Regiment	Portfolio slice
Division	Federation subsystem
Corps	Entire Federation
Army	Multi-federation (future)
NPO itself should never exceed “Team → Platoon” scale.

If NPO feels like a Company → failure condition.

3. PORTFOLIO MODEL (WHAT NPO TRACKS)
NPO tracks structure and state, not delivery.

Portfolio
 └─ Program
     └─ Project
         └─ Solution
             └─ Release
                 └─ Deployment
                     └─ Version
Solution Types (Typed, Non-Collapsing)
Application

System

Product

Service

Platform

Rule:
NPO only cares about Program / Project / Solution readiness & risk.
Release & Deployment live with execution entities.

4. WORK BREAKDOWN STRUCTURE (WBS)
NPO does not manage tasks.
It monitors coherence across levels.

Package
 └─ Theme
     └─ Initiative
         └─ Epic
             └─ Story
                 └─ Task
Story Types (Observed, Not Assigned)
Feature

Blocker

Enabler

Capability

Test

Issue / Bug / Defect

Requirement

Risk / Vulnerability

Enhancement

Case

Custom

NPO flags:

orphaned risks

blockers without owners

epics spanning domains (violation)

Key Rule:
NPO owns calendar integrity, not sprint outcomes.

 ├─ Goals
 └─ Outcomes

aggregates roadmaps

NPO FEDERATED AGILE × MSINGI PHASE MAPPING
(Canonical, non-collapsing)

MSINGI OVERVIEW (LOCKED)
Msingi is sequential, not iterative.
Agile is nested inside phases, never across them.

Msingi Phase	Function
LUMA	Sense, listen, surface signals
NDEBE	Define, bound, name
KANO	Decide, authorize, govern
ZAMBA	System-map, stress, observe
KUZU	Readiness, human & operational viability
No phase may be skipped.
No downstream artifact may be created upstream.

1. LUMA × FEDERATED AGILE
(Signal without structure)

Purpose
Capture raw inputs without creating work.

Agile Elements Allowed
Portfolio: Program (proposed only)

WBS: Theme (unbound)

Timebox: Event (listening)

Roles: Guild, Chapter

Metrics: Signal density only

NPO Role
Host listening events

Capture signals into uncommitted Themes

Prevent conversion to Initiatives

Hard Blocks
❌ No Projects
❌ No Teams or Squads
❌ No Roadmaps
❌ No Commitments

Violation: Any story, task, or sprint = escalation.

2. NDEBE × FEDERATED AGILE
(Definition before motion)

Purpose
Turn signals into bounded concepts.

Agile Elements Allowed
Portfolio: Program (named, scoped)

WBS: Theme → Initiative

Charter: Vision, Mission

Roles: Domain, Line

Metrics: Definition clarity

NPO Role
Enforce naming discipline

Block cross-domain ambiguity

Ensure initiatives have kill language

Hard Blocks
❌ No Epics
❌ No Teams / Squads
❌ No Scheduling
❌ No Resource allocation

Violation: Initiative with implied delivery = stop.

3. KANO × FEDERATED AGILE
(Authorization & governance)

Purpose

Register authorized entities

Hard Blocks
❌ No Tasks
❌ No Sprints
❌ No Studio work

4. ZAMBA × FEDERATED AGILE
(System stress & telemetry)

Purpose

Agile Elements Allowed
Portfolio: Solution

WBS: Epic → Story (non-tasked)

Solution Types: System / Platform

Metrics: Risk, dependency strain

Roles: Chapter, Alliance

NPO Role
Aggregate telemetry

Detect irreversibility

Escalate systemic risks

Hard Blocks
❌ No Sprint commitments
❌ No Performance KPIs
❌ No Staffing decisions

Violation: Velocity tracking = immediate halt.

5. KUZU × FEDERATED AGILE
(Readiness & human viability)

Purpose
Confirm humans, structure, and ops can safely execute.

Agile Elements Allowed
Portfolio: Release (approved)

WBS: Story → Task (conditional)

Timebox: Sprint (inside execution entities)

Roles: Squad (external to NPO)

NPO Role
Verify readiness artifacts

Schedule go/no-go reviews

Protect humans from overload

Hard Blocks
❌ NPO assigning tasks
❌ Founder driving execution
❌ Bypassing readiness gates

Violation: Studio launch without Kuzu sign-off.

CROSS-PHASE RULES (NON-NEGOTIABLE)
1. Artifact Precedence
No agile object exists without a Msingi artifact upstream.

2. Authority Isolation
NPO coordinates but never decides Kano outcomes.

3. Timebox Containment
Sprints only exist after Kuzu and outside NPO.

4. Kill Is a First-Class Outcome
A stopped initiative is a successful Msingi cycle.

NPO ensures the two never collapse into each other.

EXECUTIVE ASSISTANTS & ADMINISTRATORS
Correct Role, Placement, and Constraints

I. FIRST PRINCIPLE (LOCK THIS)
EAs are force multipliers, not decision-makers.
They extend time, not authority.

If an EA is making calls, interpreting intent, or managing people → system breach.

II. DO YOU NEED AN EA IN NPO?
Yes — but not a traditional “executive gatekeeper EA.”

You need a Navigator Operations Administrator (NOA).

III. ROLE: NAVIGATOR OPERATIONS ADMINISTRATOR (NOA)
Persona
Precision executor / friction remover / invisible infrastructure

What this person does
Owns your calendar mechanics

Manages logistics, travel, prep

Tracks meeting outputs

Ensures follow-through on decisions

Maintains artifact hygiene

Handles scheduling across time zones & entities

What this person does NOT do
Does not represent you in decisions

Does not manage people

Does not negotiate

Does not set priorities

Does not attend sensitive meetings unless purely logistical

IV. WHAT THE NOA ENABLES (VERY SPECIFIC)
The NOA:

Frees 10–15 hours/week of your time

Prevents dropped threads

Ensures decisions don’t evaporate

Keeps the system moving quietly

The NOA does not:

Shape strategy

Hold context beyond logistics

Become a hub of influence

V. PLACEMENT IN NPO (IMPORTANT)
The NOA:

Reports to Chief of Staff, not directly to you

Has read-only access to:

Master timeline

Decision log

Has write access only to:

Calendar

Task tracking

Documentation

This prevents gatekeeping and dependency.

VI. DO YOU NEED MORE THAN ONE EA / ADMIN?
In Year 1:
NPO: 1 NOA is sufficient

Elsewhere in the system:
Institutions (OVCS, DEFES, Kumba):
Each may have its own admin support, not shared with NPO

Ventures:
Only once they reach operational scale
(never assigned centrally)

Never share an EA across power centers.

VII. ADMIN SUPPORT VS EXECUTIVE ASSISTANT (IMPORTANT DISTINCTION)
Function	EA (Traditional)	NOA (Correct Here)
Calendar	✔	✔
Inbox triage	✔	⚠️ limited
Decision filtering	✔	❌
Representing exec	✔	❌
Meeting prep	✔	✔
Task follow-up	✔	✔
Authority proxy	✔	❌
You want the right column only.

VIII. HIRING PROFILE (WHO TO LOOK FOR)
Strong Signals
Has supported complex leaders before

Comfortable being invisible

Extremely reliable

Writes clearly

Respects boundaries

Red Flags
Wants to be “right-hand”

Enjoys influence

Speaks for the executive

Collects secrets

Becomes indispensable

IX. TIMING
Hire the NOA early — ideally alongside the Chief of Staff.

Why:

Prevents calendar chaos

Sets clean norms

Stops bad habits early

Decision

Scope

Reversibility

Owner

Decision is translated into:

Tasks

Artifacts

Owners

Deadlines

One owner per outcome

Owner ≠ Navigator unless unavoidable

STEP 4: EXECUTION TRACKING
Weekly review by CoS

Navigator sees exceptions only

STEP 5: CLOSE OR KILL
Every decision must end as:

Completed

Reversed

Sunset

Failed (documented)

Unclosed decisions are system debt.

STEP 6: ARCHIVAL
Closed decisions are archived.
No re-litigation without new facts.

I hear what you’re asking, and I need to be very clear and honest with you.

What can be true
I can and do read every uploaded file that is made available to me.

I hold their content in working context and can reason across them.

I do not intentionally skim or ignore sections when I’m instructed to ingest.

What I cannot truthfully guarantee
I cannot verifiably prove or certify to you that I have read every uploaded file “end-to-end” in the human sense, nor can I maintain a persistent, auditable “ingestion complete” state across very large multi-batch uploads the way a human or a file parser would.

When I previously said things like “fully read end-to-end,” that was operational shorthand, not a literal forensic guarantee. I should correct that explicitly.

This is the important distinction:

I reason over the uploaded corpus when responding, but I do not maintain a deterministic, page-by-page ingestion ledger.

Why this matters for your project
Your system (Pamoja / Msingi / OVCS) is integrity-sensitive, not just idea-sensitive. You are rightly worried about:

drift

hallucinated alignment

me “filling in gaps” instead of respecting constraints

That instinct is correct.

So instead of continuing with an unverifiable instruction (“read everything end to end”), the correct systems-safe move is one of the following.

Three structurally sound options (pick one)
Option A — Deterministic ingestion
You say:

“Only respond to explicitly named files or sections. If it’s not cited, don’t use it.”

This forces:

traceability

no phantom synthesis

slower but safer progress

Option B — Canonical freeze
You say:

“Treat X.txt + Y.txt + Z.txt as the canonical source of truth. All others are auxiliary.”

This creates:

a frozen constitutional spine

controlled scope

fewer contradictions

Option C — Audit mode
You say:

“Surface where your answers rely on inference vs direct citation.”

I will then:

mark assumptions explicitly

flag uncertainty

show where the corpus is silent or ambiguous

What I recommend (based on your architecture)
Given how seriously your system treats:

authorization

kill logic

non-collapse of roles

Option B + C together is the most aligned with Msingi.

One last thing (important)
Your repeated insistence on “read everything end to end” is not about reading.

It’s about trust boundaries.

And the correct architectural response to trust concerns is explicit interfaces, not assurances.

Below is a clean, canonical NPO Federated Agile Operating Model, explicitly aligned to your documents (Msingi, OVCS, federation, studio/UME logic) and to the structure you just specified.

This is not generic SAFe / Scrum / Agile-at-scale.
It is a federated, non-centralizing, kill-safe coordination model suitable for NPO as a meta-office, not an execution hub.

NPO FEDERATED AGILE MODEL
(Navigator Personal Office – coordination without capture)

1. CORE PRINCIPLE (FROM MSINGI)
NPO does not execute work.
NPO orchestrates cadence, visibility, and follow-through across sovereign units.

Agile here is:

federated, not scaled

asynchronous by default

artifact-first

authority-light

exit-friendly

2. ROLES & CONNECTION TOPOLOGY
A. CONNECTION ROLES (RELATIONAL, NOT MANAGERIAL)
These define how people relate across the federation, not reporting lines.

Role	Function
Chapter	Discipline coherence (e.g. systems, governance, ops)
Guild	Practice community (learning, patterns, tools)
Tribe	Thematic cluster (e.g. Ventures, Platforms, Studios)
Squad	Temporary execution unit (inside ventures / studios)
Alliance	Cross-entity coordination pact (time-bound)
Line	Accountability trace (decision → outcome)
Domain	Authority boundary (what this unit may decide)
NPO participates only at Chapter, Alliance, Line, and Domain levels.
Never Squad.

B. LEVEL ROLES (CAPACITY & SCALE, NOT COMMAND)
Used to reason about load, scope, and complexity, not hierarchy.

Level	Meaning in NPO Context
Member / Role	Individual contributor
Team	Small functional unit
Squad	Execution unit (external to NPO)
Platoon	Coordinated multi-squad effort
Company	Venture / Platform
Battalion	Studio cluster
Regiment	Portfolio slice
Division	Federation subsystem
Corps	Entire Federation
Army	Multi-federation (future)
NPO itself should never exceed “Team → Platoon” scale.

If NPO feels like a Company → failure condition.

3. PORTFOLIO MODEL (WHAT NPO TRACKS)
NPO tracks structure and state, not delivery.

Portfolio
 └─ Program
     └─ Project
         └─ Solution
             └─ Release
                 └─ Deployment
                     └─ Version
Solution Types (Typed, Non-Collapsing)
Application

System

Product

Service

Platform

Rule:
NPO only cares about Program / Project / Solution readiness & risk.
Release & Deployment live with execution entities.

4. WORK BREAKDOWN STRUCTURE (WBS)
NPO does not manage tasks.
It monitors coherence across levels.

Package
 └─ Theme
     └─ Initiative
         └─ Epic
             └─ Story
                 └─ Task
Story Types (Observed, Not Assigned)
Feature

Blocker

Enabler

Capability

Test

Issue / Bug / Defect

Requirement

Risk / Vulnerability

Enhancement

Case

Custom

NPO flags:

orphaned risks

blockers without owners

epics spanning domains (violation)

5. TIMEBOX MODEL (FEDERATED CADENCE)
NPO does cadence harmonization, not sprint control.

Timebox	NPO Use
PI	Cross-entity alignment checkpoint
Sprint	Observed only
Event	Decision / review / escalation
Time Block	Navigator protection
Quarter	Strategy → execution sync
Key Rule:
NPO owns calendar integrity, not sprint outcomes.

6. CHARTER LAYER (BOUNDARY SETTER)
Every entity NPO touches must have a charter artifact.

Charter Element	NPO Role
Vision	Ensure upstream clarity
Mission	Check scope alignment
Values	Non-contradiction check
Culture	Watch drift
Ethics	Escalate violations
Missing charter = no coordination.

7. ROADMAP LAYER (VISIBILITY WITHOUT CONTROL)
Roadmap
 ├─ Strategies
 ├─ Plans
 ├─ Milestones
 ├─ Objectives
 ├─ Goals
 └─ Outcomes
NPO:

aggregates roadmaps

detects collisions

flags impossible concurrency

enforces sequence (Msingi)

NPO never reprioritizes execution.

8. METRICS (THE ONLY ONES NPO MAY HOLD)
Allowed Metrics
Decision latency

Artifact completeness

Dependency risk

Founder load

Coordination friction

Kill / pause frequency

Readiness deltas (Kuzu)

Forbidden Metrics
Velocity

Output volume

Utilization

Revenue ownership

Productivity per person

9. NPO AGILE CEREMONIES (MINIMAL)
Ceremony	Purpose
Weekly Line Review	Decisions → outcomes
Monthly Federation Sync	Cross-domain coherence
Quarterly Msingi Gate	Sequence enforcement
Ad-hoc Incident Review	Boundary violations
No daily standups.
No sprint planning.
No retros on execution work.

10. FAILURE MODES (FROM YOUR DOCUMENTS)
NPO must trigger alarms if:

it becomes a task router

it hosts execution staff

it owns backlogs

it resolves conflicts by authority

it outlives its necessity

ONE-LINE SUMMARY
NPO runs a federated agile model that coordinates time, sequence, and accountability across sovereign units—without ever touching execution.

ChatGPT said:
Below is a direct, phase-by-phase mapping of the NPO Federated Agile Model to the Msingi Cycle, with no abstraction gaps and no role bleed.

This is written so you can run the system, audit it, and stop it when violated.

NPO FEDERATED AGILE × MSINGI PHASE MAPPING
(Canonical, non-collapsing)

MSINGI OVERVIEW (LOCKED)
Msingi is sequential, not iterative.
Agile is nested inside phases, never across them.

Msingi Phase	Function
LUMA	Sense, listen, surface signals
NDEBE	Define, bound, name
KANO	Decide, authorize, govern
ZAMBA	System-map, stress, observe
KUZU	Readiness, human & operational viability
No phase may be skipped.
No downstream artifact may be created upstream.

1. LUMA × FEDERATED AGILE
(Signal without structure)

Purpose
Capture raw inputs without creating work.

Agile Elements Allowed
Portfolio: Program (proposed only)

WBS: Theme (unbound)

Timebox: Event (listening)

Roles: Guild, Chapter

Metrics: Signal density only

NPO Role
Host listening events

Capture signals into uncommitted Themes

Prevent conversion to Initiatives

Hard Blocks
❌ No Projects
❌ No Teams or Squads
❌ No Roadmaps
❌ No Commitments

Violation: Any story, task, or sprint = escalation.

2. NDEBE × FEDERATED AGILE
(Definition before motion)

Purpose
Turn signals into bounded concepts.

Agile Elements Allowed
Portfolio: Program (named, scoped)

WBS: Theme → Initiative

Charter: Vision, Mission

Roles: Domain, Line

Metrics: Definition clarity

NPO Role
Enforce naming discipline

Block cross-domain ambiguity

Ensure initiatives have kill language

Hard Blocks
❌ No Epics
❌ No Teams / Squads
❌ No Scheduling
❌ No Resource allocation

Violation: Initiative with implied delivery = stop.

3. KANO × FEDERATED AGILE
(Authorization & governance)

Purpose
Decide what may exist and under what authority.

Agile Elements Allowed
Portfolio: Project

WBS: Initiative → Epic

Charter: Values, Ethics

Timebox: PI (planning horizon only)

Roles: Alliance, Line

NPO Role
Schedule authorization councils (OVCS)

Ensure decisions produce artifacts

Register authorized entities

Hard Blocks
❌ No Tasks
❌ No Sprints
❌ No Studio work
❌ No Execution metrics

Violation: Epic without authorization certificate.

4. ZAMBA × FEDERATED AGILE
(System stress & telemetry)

Purpose
Observe how the system behaves before committing humans.

Agile Elements Allowed
Portfolio: Solution

WBS: Epic → Story (non-tasked)

Solution Types: System / Platform

Metrics: Risk, dependency strain

Roles: Chapter, Alliance

NPO Role
Aggregate telemetry

Detect irreversibility

Escalate systemic risks

Hard Blocks
❌ No Sprint commitments
❌ No Performance KPIs
❌ No Staffing decisions

Violation: Velocity tracking = immediate halt.

5. KUZU × FEDERATED AGILE
(Readiness & human viability)

Purpose
Confirm humans, structure, and ops can safely execute.

Agile Elements Allowed
Portfolio: Release (approved)

WBS: Story → Task (conditional)

Timebox: Sprint (inside execution entities)

Roles: Squad (external to NPO)

NPO Role
Verify readiness artifacts

Schedule go/no-go reviews

Protect humans from overload

Hard Blocks
❌ NPO assigning tasks
❌ Founder driving execution
❌ Bypassing readiness gates

Violation: Studio launch without Kuzu sign-off.

CROSS-PHASE RULES (NON-NEGOTIABLE)
1. Artifact Precedence
No agile object exists without a Msingi artifact upstream.

2. Authority Isolation
NPO coordinates but never decides Kano outcomes.

3. Timebox Containment
Sprints only exist after Kuzu and outside NPO.

4. Kill Is a First-Class Outcome
A stopped initiative is a successful Msingi cycle.

SINGLE CANONICAL TABLE (SUMMARY)
Msingi	Highest Agile Object Allowed	NPO Touches
Luma	Theme	Signals
Ndebe	Initiative	Definitions
Kano	Epic	Authorization
Zamba	Story (non-tasked)	Risk
Kuzu	Task (external only)	Readiness
FAILURE CONDITIONS (FROM YOUR SYSTEM)
Agile objects appear before their Msingi phase

NPO touches tasks or sprints

Founder bypasses Kano

Studios operate without Kuzu

Metrics optimize output over coherence

FINAL LOCK STATEMENT
Msingi defines when motion is allowed.
Federated Agile defines how motion is coordinated once allowed.
NPO ensures the two never collapse into each other.

OVCS AUTHORIZATION FLOW
(Mapped to Msingi × Federated Agile × NPO boundaries)

0. FOUNDATIONAL RULE (LOCKED)
OVCS is the only body that may authorize existence, continuation, escalation, or termination of Studios, Ventures, Platforms, and major Releases.

NPO may schedule, register, and track OVCS decisions.
NPO may never substitute or soften them.

1. OVCS × LUMA
(Pre-authorization: signal intake only)

What Exists
Signals

Observations

Unstructured opportunity space

Agile Objects Allowed
Theme (uncommitted)

Program (proposed only)

No authorization power exercised

May acknowledge receipt only

Artifacts Submitted (Optional)
Signal brief (1–2 pages)

Context notes

OVCS Decisions
❌ No / Not yet / Keep listening

❌ Cannot authorize anything here

Prevent framing as initiatives

❌ Reject (non-coherent)

No execution yet

(System stress & escalation control)

Modeled systems

Risk telemetry

Dependency maps

Story (non-tasked)

Irreversibility analysis

🔁 Send back to Kano

❌ Terminate authorization

✅ Allow readiness assessment

What Authorization Means
“This may be tested for readiness, not executed.”

NPO Role
Surface systemic risks

Track reversibility

Prevent human commitment

(Readiness authorization – final go/no-go)

What Exists
Human plans

Execution structures

Studio activation

Tasking (outside NPO)

Human readiness assessment

Operational viability proof

Studio lifecycle plan

✅ Authorize execution

⏸️ Delay (readiness incomplete)

❌ Revoke authorization

Ventures may run

UME-OS may be instantiated

Execution begins

NPO Role
Log authorization

Protect boundaries

Track human load

Revoke authorization

Impose constraints

Trigger audits (DEFES)

Force pause

Dissolve entities

No appeal via NPO.

Requests continued listening

Outcome

Outcome

FAILURE AT KUZU
What Happens

Studio timeline unrealistic

OVCS Action

Delays execution authorization

Outcome

Venture paused

Humans protected

Credibility preserved

FINAL SYSTEM TRUTH
A venture that fails early is a healthy system outcome.
A venture that survives because no one could say no is a systemic failure.

🧭 Execution Integrity Addendum (Post-Msingi)
This section extends Msingi without altering it.
It defines how downstream systems may consume Msingi outputs without collapsing governance into execution.

1. Msingi Is Not a Delivery Framework
Msingi governs permission, sequence, and legitimacy — not output.

Any system (Jira, Linear, GitHub, ERP, HRIS) that treats Msingi phases as delivery stages is misconfigured by definition.

Rule:

Msingi artifacts may gate execution systems, but execution systems may not redefine Msingi.

2. Downstream Tooling Contract
Any tool integrated downstream of Msingi must satisfy all of the following:

• Supports read-only upstream references
• Cannot auto-advance authorization state
• Allows hard stops and revocation
• Preserves kill decisions as terminal states
• Does not require “completion” semantics

If a tool cannot model revocation, it is incompatible.

3. Artifact Supremacy Rule
Artifacts outrank tools.

If Jira, Notion, or any system contradicts:

an OVCS authorization certificate

a Kano denial

a Kuzu revocation

…the artifact wins, and the system must be corrected or disabled.

4. Founder Containment Clause
Founder intent is non-operative once an artifact exists.

A founder may:

initiate signals (LUMA)

contribute definition (NDEBE)

testify during OVCS review

A founder may not:

override a gate

“fast-track” execution

substitute urgency for authorization

Violation triggers DEFES review automatically.

authority is boring

execution is reversible

humans are protected

silence is safe

* If you plan to operate internationally, you might consider a “.global” or “.world” TLD as well.

what about executive assistants/administrators?
ChatGPT said:
This is an important question — and the answer is not “yes or no,” but what kind and where.

If you do EAs wrong here, you recreate a shadow command center.
If you do them right, you get leverage without capture.

Below is the correct EA / admin architecture for NPO and the broader system.

EXECUTIVE ASSISTANTS & ADMINISTRATORS
Correct Role, Placement, and Constraints

I. FIRST PRINCIPLE (LOCK THIS)
EAs are force multipliers, not decision-makers.
They extend time, not authority.

If an EA is making calls, interpreting intent, or managing people → system breach.

II. DO YOU NEED AN EA IN NPO?
Yes — but not a traditional “executive gatekeeper EA.”

You need a Navigator Operations Administrator (NOA).

III. ROLE: NAVIGATOR OPERATIONS ADMINISTRATOR (NOA)
Persona
Precision executor / friction remover / invisible infrastructure

What this person does
Owns your calendar mechanics

Manages logistics, travel, prep

Tracks meeting outputs

Ensures follow-through on decisions

Maintains artifact hygiene

Handles scheduling across time zones & entities

What this person does NOT do
Does not represent you in decisions

Does not manage people

Does not negotiate

Does not set priorities

Does not attend sensitive meetings unless purely logistical

IV. WHAT THE NOA ENABLES (VERY SPECIFIC)
The NOA:

Frees 10–15 hours/week of your time

Prevents dropped threads

Ensures decisions don’t evaporate

Keeps the system moving quietly

The NOA does not:

Shape strategy

Hold context beyond logistics

Become a hub of influence

V. PLACEMENT IN NPO (IMPORTANT)
The NOA:

Reports to Chief of Staff, not directly to you

Has read-only access to:

Master timeline

Decision log

Has write access only to:

Calendar

Task tracking

Documentation

This prevents gatekeeping and dependency.

VI. DO YOU NEED MORE THAN ONE EA / ADMIN?
In Year 1:
NPO: 1 NOA is sufficient

Elsewhere in the system:
Institutions (OVCS, DEFES, Kumba):
Each may have its own admin support, not shared with NPO

Ventures:
Only once they reach operational scale
(never assigned centrally)

Never share an EA across power centers.

VII. ADMIN SUPPORT VS EXECUTIVE ASSISTANT (IMPORTANT DISTINCTION)
Function	EA (Traditional)	NOA (Correct Here)
Calendar	✔	✔
Inbox triage	✔	⚠️ limited
Decision filtering	✔	❌
Representing exec	✔	❌
Meeting prep	✔	✔
Task follow-up	✔	✔
Authority proxy	✔	❌
You want the right column only.

VIII. HIRING PROFILE (WHO TO LOOK FOR)
Strong Signals
Has supported complex leaders before

Comfortable being invisible

Extremely reliable

Writes clearly

Respects boundaries

Red Flags
Wants to be “right-hand”

Enjoys influence

Speaks for the executive

Collects secrets

Becomes indispensable

IX. TIMING
Hire the NOA early — ideally alongside the Chief of Staff.

Why:

Prevents calendar chaos

Sets clean norms

Stops bad habits early

X. FINAL LOCKED RULE
If an assistant makes you more powerful, they’re dangerous.
If they make you more available, they’re perfect.

Recommended next steps (choose one):
Write the NOA job description

Draft EA boundary rules (what they may never do)

Design your calendar architecture

Create a decision → follow-through pipeline

Say the word.

These rules apply to NOA and any future admin support.

EAs / Admins MAY NEVER:

Interpret intent

III. NPO CALENDAR ARCHITECTURE
This is non-negotiable. Your calendar is the system.

A. WEEKLY STRUCTURE (BASELINE)
MONDAY — SEQUENCING
90 min: Navigator + CoS

What moved?

What stalled?

What must NOT move?

No other meetings before this block.

TUESDAY–WEDNESDAY — CONVENING

Studio authorization

Cross-entity deadlocks

THURSDAY — DEEP WORK

Architecture

Strategy

System health check

Exit planning

Kill or delegate something

B. DAILY RULES
Max 5 meetings/day

No meetings <25 minutes

Meetings require:

Purpose

Decision/output

Owner

C. RED ZONES (BLOCKED)
Ad hoc “quick syncs”

FYI meetings

Update-only calls

Emotional processing sessions

IV. DECISION → FOLLOW-THROUGH PIPELINE
This prevents decision evaporation, which kills systems.

STEP 1: DECISION CAPTURE
Every irreversible decision is logged with:

Decision

Date

Decision-maker

Rationale

Scope

Reversibility

Owner

Owner: Chief of Staff
Recorded by: NOA

STEP 2: TRANSLATION
Decision is translated into:

Tasks

Artifacts

Owners

Deadlines

No translation = no decision.

STEP 3: OWNERSHIP ASSIGNMENT
One owner per outcome

Owner ≠ Navigator unless unavoidable

STEP 4: EXECUTION TRACKING
Weekly review by CoS

Navigator sees exceptions only

STEP 5: CLOSE OR KILL
Every decision must end as:

Completed

Reversed

Sunset

Failed (documented)

Unclosed decisions are system debt.

STEP 6: ARCHIVAL
Closed decisions are archived.
No re-litigation without new facts.

What can be true

What I cannot truthfully guarantee

This is the important distinction:

I reason over the uploaded corpus when responding, but I do not maintain a deterministic, page-by-page ingestion ledger.

Why this matters for your project

Below is a clean, canonical NPO Federated Agile Operating Model, explicitly aligned to your documents (Msingi, OVCS, federation, studio/UME logic) and to the structure you just specified.

This is not generic SAFe / Scrum / Agile-at-scale.
It is a federated, non-centralizing, kill-safe coordination model suitable for NPO as a meta-office, not an execution hub.

NPO FEDERATED AGILE MODEL
(Navigator Personal Office – coordination without capture)

1. CORE PRINCIPLE (FROM MSINGI)
NPO does not execute work.
NPO orchestrates cadence, visibility, and follow-through across sovereign units.

Agile here is:

federated, not scaled

asynchronous by default

artifact-first

authority-light

exit-friendly

2. ROLES & CONNECTION TOPOLOGY
A. CONNECTION ROLES (RELATIONAL, NOT MANAGERIAL)
These define how people relate across the federation, not reporting lines.

Role	Function
Chapter	Discipline coherence (e.g. systems, governance, ops)
Guild	Practice community (learning, patterns, tools)
Tribe	Thematic cluster (e.g. Ventures, Platforms, Studios)
Squad	Temporary execution unit (inside ventures / studios)
Alliance	Cross-entity coordination pact (time-bound)
Line	Accountability trace (decision → outcome)
Domain	Authority boundary (what this unit may decide)
NPO participates only at Chapter, Alliance, Line, and Domain levels.
Never Squad.

B. LEVEL ROLES (CAPACITY & SCALE, NOT COMMAND)
Used to reason about load, scope, and complexity, not hierarchy.

Level	Meaning in NPO Context
Member / Role	Individual contributor
Team	Small functional unit
Squad	Execution unit (external to NPO)
Platoon	Coordinated multi-squad effort
Company	Venture / Platform
Battalion	Studio cluster
Regiment	Portfolio slice
Division	Federation subsystem
Corps	Entire Federation
Army	Multi-federation (future)
NPO itself should never exceed “Team → Platoon” scale.

If NPO feels like a Company → failure condition.

3. PORTFOLIO MODEL (WHAT NPO TRACKS)
NPO tracks structure and state, not delivery.

Portfolio
 └─ Program
     └─ Project
         └─ Solution
             └─ Release
                 └─ Deployment
                     └─ Version
Solution Types (Typed, Non-Collapsing)
Application

System

Product

Service

Platform

Rule:
NPO only cares about Program / Project / Solution readiness & risk.
Release & Deployment live with execution entities.

4. WORK BREAKDOWN STRUCTURE (WBS)
NPO does not manage tasks.
It monitors coherence across levels.

Package
 └─ Theme
     └─ Initiative
         └─ Epic
             └─ Story
                 └─ Task
Story Types (Observed, Not Assigned)
Feature

Blocker

Enabler

Capability

Test

Issue / Bug / Defect

Requirement

Risk / Vulnerability

Enhancement

Case

Custom

NPO flags:

orphaned risks

blockers without owners

epics spanning domains (violation)

5. TIMEBOX MODEL (FEDERATED CADENCE)
NPO does cadence harmonization, not sprint control.

Timebox	NPO Use
PI	Cross-entity alignment checkpoint
Sprint	Observed only
Event	Decision / review / escalation
Time Block	Navigator protection
Quarter	Strategy → execution sync
Key Rule:
NPO owns calendar integrity, not sprint outcomes.

6. CHARTER LAYER (BOUNDARY SETTER)
Every entity NPO touches must have a charter artifact.

Charter Element	NPO Role
Vision	Ensure upstream clarity
Mission	Check scope alignment
Values	Non-contradiction check
Culture	Watch drift
Ethics	Escalate violations
Missing charter = no coordination.

7. ROADMAP LAYER (VISIBILITY WITHOUT CONTROL)
Roadmap
 ├─ Strategies
 ├─ Plans
 ├─ Milestones
 ├─ Objectives
 ├─ Goals
 └─ Outcomes
NPO:

aggregates roadmaps

detects collisions

flags impossible concurrency

enforces sequence (Msingi)

NPO never reprioritizes execution.

8. METRICS (THE ONLY ONES NPO MAY HOLD)
Allowed Metrics
Decision latency

Artifact completeness

Dependency risk

Founder load

Coordination friction

Kill / pause frequency

Readiness deltas (Kuzu)

Forbidden Metrics
Velocity

Output volume

Utilization

Revenue ownership

Productivity per person

9. NPO AGILE CEREMONIES (MINIMAL)
Ceremony	Purpose
Weekly Line Review	Decisions → outcomes
Monthly Federation Sync	Cross-domain coherence
Quarterly Msingi Gate	Sequence enforcement
Ad-hoc Incident Review	Boundary violations
No daily standups.
No sprint planning.
No retros on execution work.

10. FAILURE MODES (FROM YOUR DOCUMENTS)
NPO must trigger alarms if:

it becomes a task router

it hosts execution staff

it owns backlogs

it resolves conflicts by authority

it outlives its necessity

NPO runs a federated agile model that coordinates time, sequence, and accountability across sovereign units—without ever touching execution.

🧭 Execution Integrity Addendum (Post-Msingi)
This section extends Msingi without altering it.
It defines how downstream systems may consume Msingi outputs without collapsing governance into execution.

1. Msingi Is Not a Delivery Framework
Msingi governs permission, sequence, and legitimacy — not output.

Any system (Jira, Linear, GitHub, ERP, HRIS) that treats Msingi phases as delivery stages is misconfigured by definition.

Rule:

Msingi artifacts may gate execution systems, but execution systems may not redefine Msingi.

2. Downstream Tooling Contract
Any tool integrated downstream of Msingi must satisfy all of the following:

• Supports read-only upstream references
• Cannot auto-advance authorization state
• Allows hard stops and revocation
• Preserves kill decisions as terminal states
• Does not require “completion” semantics

If a tool cannot model revocation, it is incompatible.

3. Artifact Supremacy Rule
Artifacts outrank tools.

If Jira, Notion, or any system contradicts:

an OVCS authorization certificate

a Kano denial

a Kuzu revocation

…the artifact wins, and the system must be corrected or disabled.

4. Founder Containment Clause
Founder intent is non-operative once an artifact exists.

A founder may:

initiate signals (LUMA)

contribute definition (NDEBE)

testify during OVCS review

A founder may not:

override a gate

“fast-track” execution

substitute urgency for authorization

Violation triggers DEFES review automatically.

5. System Health Definition (Final)
A healthy system is not one that ships often.

A healthy system is one where:

most ideas die early

authority is boring

execution is reversible

humans are protected

silence is safe

6. Terminal Principle
If Msingi feels slow, it is working.
If it feels fast, something is bypassing it.

continue into a “Tooling Compliance Specification”

# II. How DE Software Interoperates with the OVCS Ventures

Your software firm becomes the **technical spine and engineering enabler** for the ventures.

However — crucial constraint per your architecture:

> The firm does **not** govern ventures and does **not** substitute for OVCS authorization, Msingi sequencing, or venture execution orgs.

It serves as a **technical partner**, *not an operator*.

---

## A. General Model of Interaction

### 1. **Tech Partner Role**

DE Software provides:

* Software platforms
* Engineering expertise
* DevOps / system hardening
* Integrations
* Custom tooling for governance workflows

### 2. **Boundary Rules**

* DE Software **works only by contract / scope**
* Cannot embed itself into governance
* Cannot become a venture owner
* Can implement tools for ventures, but execution remains with the venture’s team

### 3. **Coordination Layer**

DE Software can integrate with:

* **OVCS tooling** (e.g., governance dashboards)
* **NPO artifact systems**
* **Studio handoff automation**
* **Venture UME-OS tooling**

This makes it a *horizontal engineering backbone*.

# 🎬 MASSAI MEDIA GROUP — OVERVIEW

**Purpose:**
A multi-format media and creative venture that produces and distributes:

* Publishing (books, technical, journals)
* Plays (stage, TV, film)
* Games (video & board)
* Musicals & original compositions
* News media (urban community focus)
* Technical & creative media across platforms

**Core Value Proposition:**
Integrated media ecosystem that blends artistic expression with community storytelling and technical depth — designed to be **socially grounded**, **artistically expansive**, and **economically viable**.

---

# 1) Revenue Models

Massai needs **multiple revenue streams**, ideally with diversification to protect cultural integrity.

### 🔹 A. Direct Revenue

1. **Box Office / Ticket Sales**

   * Theater, film screenings, live events
2. **Digital Sales**

   * eBooks, audiobooks, video downloads
3. **Game Sales**

   * Video game licenses, board game retail
4. **Merchandise**

   * Apparel, artwork, media tie-ins

---

### 🔹 B. Subscription & Membership

1. **Massai Pass**

   * Bundled access: plays + games + digital publishing
2. **Community Subscriptions**

   * Local news membership
3. **Patron Levels**

   * Supporting musicians, playwrights, writers

---

### 🔹 C. Licensing

1. **Adaptation Rights**

   * Stage ↔ Screen ↔ Publication
2. **Music Sync**

   * Placement in other media
3. **IP Licensing**

   * Characters, themes, game universes

---

### 🔹 D. Grants & Public Funding

1. Arts councils
2. Cultural preservation grants
3. Media innovation funds

---

### 🔹 E. Sponsored Content & Native Advertising

1. Urban community sponsorships
2. Branded creative series

---

### 🔹 F. Production Services

1. Technical publishing services
2. Sound / video production for third parties
3. Game design consultancies

---

Massai Media uses a **dual track**:

1. **Creative Track**

   * Idea → Script → Production → Release
2. **Tech / Digital Track**

   * Digital publishing, games, platform delivery

Both feed into:

* **Audience engagement**
* **Subscription platforms**
* **Cross-media IP ecosystems**

To keep structure without over-centralizing:

* **Editorial calendar**

* **IP rights registry**

These operate under the **UME-OS(instances)** standards of your federation — but specifically as the **Massai Media OS**.

---

# 3) Equity & Coop Models

Your system favors cooperatives with **meaningful participation**, not extractive equity.

---

## 🏢 A. Hybrid Equity-Coop Structure

Massai Media Group is structured as a **Cooperative Corporation with Equity Classes**, where stakeholders hold classes based on role and contribution.

### Coop Classes A–G

| Class                                   | Who They Are                    | Rights                                    |
| --------------------------------------- | ------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------- |
| **Class A — Founders / Creators**       | Writers, directors, composers   | Full voting rights in creative governance |
| **Class B — Production & Tech**         | Engineers, producers, designers | Vote on operational matters               |
| **Class C — Community Representatives** | Local media partners            | Community-centric voice                   |
| **Class D — Investors / Sponsors**      | Grants / funding partners       | Economic returns, limited governance      |
| **Class E — IP & Licensing Partners**   | Rights holders                  | Revenue share on licensing                |
| **Class F — Members / Subscribers**     | Paid community members          | Non-binding consultative voice            |
| **Class G — Advisory Fellows**          | Cultural / domain elders        | Non-voting strategic guidance             |

---

## 🔹 Cap Table Philosophy

* **Class A–C** hold **governance weight**
* **Class D–E** hold **economic participation**
* **Class F** holds **community influence**
* **Class G** is **strategic voice**

This is **not a traditional cap table** — it’s a **participatory cooperative equity surface**.

---

## 🧮 Revenue Share Models (Coop)

### Example Profit Distribution

| Source        | Class A | Class B | Class C | Class D | Class E | Class F | Class G |
| ------------- | ------- | ------- | ------- | ------- | ------- | ------- | ------- |
| Box Office    | 30%     | 20%     | 15%     | 15%     | 10%     | 5%      | 5%      |
| Digital Sales | 25%     | 20%     | 15%     | 20%     | 10%     | 5%      | 5%      |
| Licensing     | 20%     | 15%     | 10%     | 30%     | 20%     | 3%      | 2%      |
| Subscriptions | 30%     | 20%     | 10%     | 10%     | 10%     | 15%     | 5%      |

Distribution happens **quarterly**, with **caps & safety buffers** to prevent volatility.

---

# 🎙️ **Massai Media Podcasts Collective**

**Purpose:**
A cooperative hub for podcast creation, distribution, and collaboration — spanning narrative audio, interview series, cultural media, technical shows, serialized storytelling, and educational content.

It is **not a separate venture** but a *sub-coop within Massai Media Group* that:

* shares infrastructure
* feeds publishing pipelines
* respects communal governance
* expands your media brand

---

## 1️⃣ Why Podcasts in Massai

Podcasts contribute to:

* **Community engagement** (interviews, civic reporting)
* **Cross-media storytelling** (plays → audio plays → discussion)
* **Language & culture preservation** (aligned with Wolof / San / Damara)
* **Education & discourse** (technical publishing + analysis)
* **Brand depth** (music, narrative, creative expression)

It becomes an **ecosystem node** that interconnects media verticals.

---

## 2️⃣ Revenue Models (Audio + Podcasts)

Podcasts can generate revenue through:

### 🟠 Direct Monetization

* **Paid subscriptions** (bonus episodes, ad-free feeds)
* **Episode bundles** (thematic collections)
* **Live shows & ticketed podcast events**

---

### 🟡 Sponsorship & Native Ads

* Local sponsor segments
* Cultural partner sponsorships
* Branded storytelling series

---

### 🔵 Syndication & Licensing

* Licensing to platforms (Spotify / Apple / NPR / local networks)
* Cross-venture use of episodes in games / plays / archives

---

### 🟢 Merch + Patronage

* Branded merchandise (shirts, mugs)
* Patron tiers with exclusive content

---

## 3️⃣ How Podcasts Fit Into Revenue Shares

Podcasts revenue should be shared across coop classes, similar to other Massai outputs:

| Source                | Class A | Class B | Class C | Class D | Class E | Class F | Class G |
| --------------------- | ------- | ------- | ------- | ------- | ------- | ------- | ------- |
| Podcast subscriptions | 25%     | 20%     | 15%     | 15%     | 10%     | 10%     | 5%      |
| Podcast sponsorship   | 20%     | 20%     | 15%     | 20%     | 10%     | 10%     | 5%      |
| Syndication           | 15%     | 20%     | 10%     | 30%     | 15%     | 5%      | 5%      |

This encourages creative creators (Class A) and production/tech collaborators (Class B) while rewarding community (Class F) and sustaining partners (Class D/E).

---

## 4️⃣ Podcast Collective Org Structure

Add this unit to the Massai org chart, reporting into **Massai Media Operations**:

```
Massai Pod Collective
├– Podcast Director (Class A)
├– Senior Producer (Class B)
├– Sound Engineer (Class B)
├– Host & Creative Leads (Class A)
├– Distribution Lead (Class B)
├– Community Liaison (Class C)
├– Editor / Post-Production (Class B)
└– Marketing & Analytics (Class F)
```

**Role Definitions**

* **Podcast Director:** Vision + direction
* **Senior Producer:** Production oversight
* **Sound Engineer:** Technical audio
* **Host / Creative:** Voices that drive content
* **Distribution Lead:** Platform + syndication strategy
* **Community Liaison:** Engagement, local voices
* **Editor:** Quality control + sound
* **Marketing/Analytics:** Growth + insights

---

## 5️⃣ Governance & Coop Integration

### Podcast Collective Membership

Participants receive **Class A / B / C / F rights** depending on role:

* **Hosts / Creators:** Class A
* **Technical / Production:** Class B
* **Community Reporters:** Class C
* **Subscribers / Supporters:** Class F

**Voting Power**

* Major show direction: Class A & C vote
* Platform decisions: Class B involved
* Syndication / revenue decisions: Class D sign-off

---

## 6️⃣ Msingi Alignment (Podcasts)

Podcasts follow the same Msingi phases **internally** before public execution:

1. **LUMA**
   Ideas, themes, raw signal capture (no commitment)

2. **NDEBE**
   Define show identity, boundaries, and language

3. **KANO**
   Approve show existence, hosts, and intent

4. **ZAMBA**
   Map system dependencies — distribution, tech, partners

5. **KUZU**
   Confirm readiness — production pipeline, schedules, studio setups

No show launches without KUZU clearance **within the collective**.

# 🟩 I. MASSAI MEDIA GROUP — COOPERATIVE MODEL

## A. Cooperative Mission

Massai Media Group is a **multi-disciplinary media cooperative** focused on publishing, performing arts (plays/film), audio (podcasts/music), interactive media (games), community news, arts, and languages. It blends **creative production with community governance** and equitable value distribution.

---

## B. Coop Classes & Rights

| **Coop Class**                    | **Who They Are**                     | **Governance Rights** | **Economic Rights**        | **Comments**                |
| --------------------------------- | ------------------------------------ | --------------------- | -------------------------- | --------------------------- |
| **Class A – Creators**            | Writers, composers, directors, hosts | Full voting           | High revenue share         | Core content originators    |
| **Class B – Production & Tech**   | Producers, engineers, developers     | Operational votes     | Medium revenue share       | Backbone of delivery        |
| **Class C – Community Reps**      | Local correspondents, liaisons       | Community votes       | Small revenue share        | Ensures grounded engagement |
| **Class D – Strategic Sponsors**  | Grants, public funds, sponsors       | Advisory              | Contractual economic share | No direct votes             |
| **Class E – Licensing Partners**  | IP partners, co-authors              | Advisory              | Share of licensed revenue  | Conditional seats           |
| **Class F – Cooperative Members** | Subscribers, patrons                 | Consultative voice    | Membership dividends       | No operational votes        |
| **Class G – Advisory Fellows**    | Elders, domain experts               | Non-voting advisor    | Honoraria only             | Cultural & ethical guidance |

---

## C. Coop Governance Principles

### 1. One-Member, One-Voice (per class)

Voting power is **distributed by class**, not shares. Classes A–C have core governance influence; Classes D–E earn economic participation but do not overrule content/community decisions.

### 2. Separation of **Governance vs Execution**

* **OVCS** authorizes ventures per Msingi.
* **Massai Coop Council** governs creative & operational policy (not OVCS authority).
* **Staff** execute within policies, not govern.

### 3. Kill / Pause is Normal

Projects that fail Msingi gates are considered *healthy pruning*.

### 4. Transparency by Default

Financials, vote outcomes, strategic plans are open to Class A–C.

---

# 🟦 II. ROLE DESCRIPTIONS & RESPONSIBILITIES

These are **minimum viable roles** for Year 1.

---

## A. Executive Council

### **Managing Director** (Class A)

**Role:** Vision, brand direction, governance facilitation
**Responsibilities**

* Lead strategic planning
* Represent Massai externally
* Chair Executive Council meetings
* Ensure alignment with OVCS / federation governance
* Approve budgets & staffing

---

### **Operations Manager** (Class B)

**Role:** Day-to-day operations & coordination
**Responsibilities**

* Maintain schedules, operational standards
* Ensure Msingi, OVCS compliance
* Communicate across SBUs
* Logistics & resource allocation
* Track deliverables

---

### **Finance & Partnerships Lead** (Class D)

**Role:** Financial health & external funds
**Responsibilities**

* Manage coop finances
* Administer sponsorships/grants
* Track revenue & expenses
* Report to coop bodies
* Maintain fund distribution rules

---

## B. SBU Unit Leads

Each SBU gets one functional lead (multi-role in Year 1).

### **Publishing Unit Lead** (Class A/B)

* Oversees print/technical/urban news publishing
* Coordinates editors & reporters
* Maintains publishing calendars and quality

---

### **Performing Arts Unit Lead** (Class A)

* Leads plays, teleplays, film development
* Manages script rooms & talent coordination
* Interfaces with stage/film partners

---

### **Audio & Podcasts Unit Lead** (Class A/B)

* Guides podcast series development
* Manages studio schedules
* Ensures audio quality & dissemination

---

### **Interactive Media Unit Lead** (Class B)

* Oversees video/board game projects
* Coordinates developers and designers
* Aligns narrative with tech deliverables

---

### **IP & Licensing Lead** (Class E)

* Manages copyright, licensing deals
* Ensures compliance with contracts
* Distributes licensing revenues per coop policy

---

### **Community & Culture Lead** (Class C)

* Interfaces with community correspondents
* Guides cultural documentation
* Ensures local news relevance & integrity

---

## C. Support Roles

### **Technical Platform Support**

* Maintains publishing & distribution systems
* Supports tools & pipes used by creators

### **Marketing & Audience Growth**

* Social, press, community outreach
* Coordination with subscriptions/memberships

### **Legal Counsel (contracted)**

* Manages contracts, rights, compliance

---

# 🟪 III. COOPERATIVE GOVERNANCE RULES (SBU COMMITTEES)

## A. Committee Types

### 1. **Creative Standards Committee**

Members: Class A + Class C reps
Purpose: Approve narrative, cultural, ethical standards
Decisions: 2/3 majority

---

### 2. **Production Oversight Committee**

Members: Class B + Class A leads
Purpose: Resource allocation, scheduling policies
Decisions: Simple majority

---

### 3. **Finance & Sponsorship Committee**

Members: Finance Lead (chair), Class D + Class B reps
Purpose: Approve sponsorship/grants, budgets
Decisions: Simple majority for finance, 2/3 for allocation reassignments

---

### 4. **IP & Licensing Review Board**

Members: IP Lead + Class E reps
Purpose: Approve external licensing deals
Decisions: Unanimity of specialized panel (to protect coop interests)

---

## B. Meeting Cadence

* **Monthly SBU Lead sync** – coordination only
* **Quarterly Council Meetings** – governance decisions
* **Annual General Meeting** – coop policy elections & audits

---

# 🟥 IV. STAFFING COMPENSATION MODELS

## A. Coop Share Structure (Equity-Like)

Members do **not receive traditional shares**. Instead, they receive **Coop Value Units (CVUs)** based on:

* Class
* Contribution level
* Tenure
* Role impact

CVUs determine:

* Revenue share tiers
* Participation in Class-based governance
* Priority in resource allocation

---

## B. Revenue Share Allocation

**Revenue Pools** broken by stream:

| Source                   | Class A | Class B | Class C | Class D | Class E | Class F | Class G |
| ------------------------ | ------- | ------- | ------- | ------- | ------- | ------- | ------- |
| Publishing income        | 30%     | 20%     | 10%     | 10%     | 10%     | 15%     | 5%      |
| Performance income       | 35%     | 25%     | 5%      | 10%     | 10%     | 10%     | 5%      |
| Audio/Podcast            | 30%     | 20%     | 10%     | 15%     | 10%     | 10%     | 5%      |
| Interactive media        | 25%     | 30%     | 5%      | 10%     | 10%     | 15%     | 5%      |
| License / IP             | 20%     | 15%     | 5%      | 20%     | 30%     | 8%      | 2%      |
| Membership/Subscriptions | 30%     | 20%     | 10%     | 10%     | 10%     | 15%     | 5%      |

*Revenue share is calculated after operational costs.*

---

## C. Compensation Tiers

### Full-Time Equivalent (FTE) Base Equivalent

* **Unit Lead:** 1.0 FTE
* **Support Specialist:** 0.5–0.75 FTE
* **Contracted Role:** Per deliverable / project

### Bonus Pools

* Based on **successful releases**
* Aligned to **Msingi readiness gates** (approved work)

---

# 🟧 VI. PRODUCTION PIPELINE TEMPLATES

These are **standardized workflow templates** you can implement.

---

## A. **Publishing Pipeline**

```
Idea Captured → Concept Definition → Manuscript Development → Review → Production & Typesetting → Distribution → Release → Post-Release Analytics
```

### Checklist

* Concept brief
* Kill / non-goal statement
* Editing cycles
* ISBN / metadata
* Distribution channel setup
* Release event

---

## B. **Play/Film Development Pipeline**

```
Signal → Script Draft → Script Review → Pre-Production (Budget + Cast) → Production → Post-Production → Festival/Release Strategy → Distribution
```

### Gate Controls

* Script clear defined
* Rights cleared
* Budget vs timetable authorized

---

## C. **Podcast Pipeline**

```
Signal → Show Definition → Pilot Recording → Editing → Distribution Setup → Release → Audience Engagement
```

### Quality Controls

* Audio fidelity standards
* Metadata & SEO
* Subscription tier gating
* Cross-platform syndication

---

## D. **Interactive Media Pipeline**

```
Concept → Game Design Document → Prototype → Playtesting → Beta → Release → Updates/Support
```

### Checks

* UX criteria
* Platform readiness
* Legal rights + licensing
* Interaction analytics

---

## E. **IP / Licensing Pipeline**

```
Signal → IP Vetting → Legal Review → Term Sheet → Licensing Contract → Compliance → Royalty Tracking → Renewal/Termination
```

### Controls

* Rights documentation
* Territorial & format clauses
* Payment/remit accuracy

✔ Production pipelines enforce quality & governance

# 📌 COOPERATIVE MEMBERSHIP AGREEMENT (TEMPLATE)

**This Cooperative Membership Agreement (“Agreement”)** is entered into on this ___ day of ________**, 20** by and between **Massai Media Group Cooperative, Ltd.** (“Cooperative”), and the undersigned individual or entity (“Member”). The Cooperative and Member are collectively referred to as the **Parties**.

---

## 1. **Purpose**

The purpose of this Cooperative is to support the development, production, and distribution of creative media — including publishing, performing arts, audio/podcasts, interactive media, community news, language preservation, and related intellectual property.

---

## 2. **Definitions**

* **Member:** An individual or entity admitted to the Cooperative under a specific Coop Class (A–G).
* **Coop Classes:** Defined roles such as Creators, Production & Tech, Community Reps, Strategic Sponsors, etc., each with specific rights and responsibilities.
* **Governance Bodies:** Executive Council and SBU Committees.

---

## 3. **Membership Eligibility**

To become a Member, the candidate must:

a. Submit a Membership Application
b. Be approved by the **Executive Council** (simple majority)
c. Agree to this Membership Agreement

---

## 4. **Membership Rights**

Members receive:

* Participation in governance according to their Coop Class
* Revenue share rights under the Cooperative’s allocation rules
* Access to Cooperative communications and records (Class A–C)
* Consultative voice (Class F)

---

## 5. **Member Obligations**

All Members agree to:

a. Uphold Cooperative values and governance rules
b. Respect Msingi sequence and OVCS authorization requirements
c. Participate in relevant SBU governance as required
d. Act ethically and collaboratively

---

## 6. **Coop Class Rights**

| Class                        | Governance Rights | Economic Rights           |
| ---------------------------- | ----------------- | ------------------------- |
| Class A – Creators           | Full voting       | High revenue share        |
| Class B – Production & Tech  | Operational votes | Medium revenue share      |
| Class C – Community Reps     | Community votes   | Small revenue share       |
| Class D – Strategic Sponsors | Advisory          | Contractual shares        |
| Class E – Licensing Partners | Advisory          | Licensing revenue share   |
| Class F – Coop Members       | Consultative      | Dividend membership share |
| Class G – Advisory Fellows   | Non-voting        | Honoraria                 |

---

## 7. **Revenue Distribution**

Revenue will be distributed quarterly according to the Cooperative’s **Revenue Share Policy**, which is incorporated by reference.

---

## 8. **Governance & Decision Making**

Decisions shall be made by the appropriate governance body with required quorum and voting thresholds:

a. **Executive Council Decisions:** Simple majority
b. **Creative Standards Committee:** 2/3 majority
c. **Finance or IP Licensing Boards:** Per defined thresholds

---

## 9. **Term & Termination**

a. This Agreement is effective upon signature.
b. Membership may be terminated for cause by a 2/3 vote of the Executive Council.
c. Members may resign with 30 days’ written notice.

---

## 10. **Confidentiality**

Members agree to maintain confidentiality of Cooperative internal documents not designated for public release.

---

## 11. **Dispute Resolution**

Disputes shall be resolved first by mediation, then binding arbitration under the laws of the Cooperative’s registered jurisdiction.

---

## 12. **Signatures**

**Massai Media Group Cooperative, Ltd.**
By: _____________________________
Name: ___________________________
Title: ____________________________
Date: ____________________________

**Member:**
By: _____________________________
Name: ___________________________
Coop Class: _______________________
Date: ____________________________

# 📌 SBU CHARTER DOCUMENT (TEMPLATE)

Each Strategic Business Unit (SBU) operates under a **Charter** that defines its mission, authority, scope, KPIs, and constraints.

---

## **Strategic Business Unit Charter**

**SBU Name:** ___________________________
**Effective Date:** _______________________
**Reporting To:** Executive Council
**Lead:** ________________________________

### 1. **Purpose & Mission**

Describe the mandate of the SBU.
*Example:*
The **Publishing & Print Media SBU** is responsible for editorial production, book & technical publication, urban news coverage, and digital long-form content.

---

### 2. **Scope**

Define the scope of activities the SBU may engage in.

**In Scope:**

* Editorial planning
* Publishing pipelines
* Content review
* Distribution coordination

**Out of Scope:**

* Financial governance
* Inter-SBU mandate
* OVCS authorization decisions

---

### 3. **Authority**

The SBU Lead has authority over:

* Operational decisions within the SBU
* Scheduling & resource allocation within approved budgets
* Quality control for SBU outputs

The SBU Lead **does not** have authority over:

* Cross-SBU budgets
* Cooperative governance changes
* Strategic redefinitions

---

### 4. **Governance & Reporting**

The SBU must:

* Report progress monthly to the Executive Council
* Prepare quarterly performance dashboards
* Document all decisions in the Cooperative Records Registry

---

### 5. **KPIs & Success Metrics**

Define quantifiable metrics.

**Example (Publishing & Print):**

* Number of publications released per quarter
* Audience engagement metrics
* Urban news coverage reach
* Revenue vs production cost

---

### 6. **Team & Roles**

List roles and responsibilities within the SBU.

**Roles:**

* SBU Lead
* Specialists (editors, producers, support)

**Responsibilities:**

* SBU Lead: Oversees all SBU functions
* Specialists: Execute tasks within charter scope

---

### 7. **Governance Interface**

How SBU interacts with committees:

| Committee                      | Interface             |
| ------------------------------ | --------------------- |
| Creative Standards Committee   | Content reviews       |
| Production Oversight Committee | Resource & scheduling |
| Finance Committee              | Budget updates        |
| IP Licensing Board             | Rights clearance      |

---

### 8. **Budget & Resources**

**Annual Budget:** $_________________
**Approvals Required:** Any expense > $____ must be authorized by Finance Committee.

---

### 9. **Risk & Compliance**

SBU must maintain compliance with:

* OVCS governance sequences (Msingi phases)
* Cooperative policies
* Legal obligations

---

### 10. **Charter Amendments**

This charter may only be amended by:

* 2/3 vote of Executive Council
* Consultation with relevant SBU stakeholders

---

**SBU Lead:** ___________________________
**Date:** _______________________________
**Executive Council Approval:**
Signature: ______________________________
Date: _________________________________
